Sound Is an Accident, Not a Body
Refutation of touch perception and that sound is a body

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why classical Islamic theologians argued that sound is an accident, not a body, based on the phenomenon of many people hearing the same sound simultaneously.

Core Idea
Sound is an accident: it cannot be in many ears as a body would.

In this passage, the author tackles two related Mu'tazili claims: that senses perceive by physical touch, and that sound is a body that travels into the ear. While the first is quickly dismissed as baseless, the second receives a detailed refutation. By analyzing how sound is experienced by a crowd, the author demonstrates that sound must be an accident, not a material body.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice how the author dismisses the first claim and then focuses on the second.
The Arabic may contain a word 'اكتشفوه' which is likely 'اكتنفوه' (surrounded); the meaning is clear.
2
Identify the two refuted claims
The passage begins by rejecting the idea that senses perceive through touch (المماسة). Then it rejects that sound is a body (جسم) that moves and enters the ear. See how the author links them.
3
Understand the argument against sound as a body
The author argues that sound falls under the definition of accidents (أعراض), and accidents cannot transfer from place to place or enter a locus because that is a property of bodies.
This is a key principle in Islamic atomism: accidents are non-substantial and do not move.
4
Examine the proof of simultaneous hearing
The author provides a thought experiment: a man speaks in front of a thousand people, and everyone hears the same sound in its entirety. If sound were a body, it could not occupy many places at once. Also, each person hears the whole sound, not a part.
This is a decisive argument: bodies cannot be multiplied in different locations while remaining identical.
5
Reflect on the intuition used
The author appeals to 'بديهة العقل' (intuition of the mind) that each person hears the full sound. This shows the argument is based on immediate rational insight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودعواه أن الحواس تدرك بطريق المماسة، دعوى متعرية عن البرهان بل هو باطل، وقد فرغنا الآن عن إبطاله، ثم هو باطل بالسمع. وقوله: إن الصوت جسم ينتقل فيدخل في صماخ السامع باطل، لدخول الصوت تحت حد الأعراض على ما قررنا قبل هذا في أثناء كلامنا، ولا يتصور من الأعراض الانتقال من محل إلى محل ودخولها في محل لأن ذلك من صفات الأجسام. والذي يحقق هذا أن الرجل إذا وجد منه صوت بحضرة ألف نفر اكتشفوه من جوانبه الأربع يسمع كل واحد منهم ذلك الصوت بعينه بكماله، ولا يتصور دخول الجسم في أمكنة كثيرة ، ولا يقال : يسمع كل واحد منهم بعضه لأن كل عاقل يعرف ببديهة عقله أنه يسمع كمال صوته ولا يقال : يسمع كل واحد منهم صوتا على حدة.
And his claim that the senses perceive by way of touch is a claim devoid of proof; rather it is false, and we have just finished refuting it. Then it is false by hearing. And his statement that sound is a body that transfers and enters the ear canal of the hearer is false, because sound falls under the definition of accidents as we have established before this in the course of our speech. It is inconceivable for accidents to transfer from locus to locus and to enter into a locus, because that is among the properties of bodies. And what verifies this is that when a man produces a sound in the presence of a thousand people who surround him from his four sides, each one of them hears that same sound in its entirety. It is inconceivable for a body to enter into many places. Nor is it said that each one of them hears a part of it, because every rational person knows by the intuition of his mind that he hears the entirety of his sound. And it is not said that each one of them hears a separate sound.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage refutes two related Mu'tazili claims: (1) that senses perceive via touch, and (2) that sound is a body that travels into the ear. The author dismisses the first as baseless. For the second, he argues that sound is an accident, and accidents cannot move from place to place or enter a locus. He provides a clear proof: when a man speaks in front of a crowd, everyone hears the same sound in full simultaneously. If sound were a body, it could not be in many ears at once; moreover, each hears the whole sound, not a part. This demonstrates that sound is an accident and not a material body.

Key Terms

الحواس
الصوت
الجسم
العرض
الانتقال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sound is a physical body that travels through the air and enters the ear.
Correction: Sound is an accident (non-material) that does not move; the same sound is heard in its entirety by many people simultaneously, which would be impossible for a body.

Checkpoint
What argument does the author use to prove that sound is not a body?
A) Sound is invisible
B) A single sound is heard by many people simultaneously in its entirety
C) Sound causes pain
D) Sound is created by God

Key Takeaway
Sound is an accident, not a body, because many people can hear the same sound in full at once, which is impossible for a material body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the call to prayer or the recitation of the Quran, do you realize that what you are hearing is not a physical body traveling through the air, but an accident that Allah creates for you to perceive? How does this truth affect your attentiveness? This very day, pause during an adhan or a verse and remind yourself: this sound is not a thing that moves; it is a sign from Allah that He gives you fully. Will you do that?
?
If sound were a body, each person could only hear a part of it. But you hear the entire lecture, the entire verse. Has this reality ever struck you as a mercy from Allah? Reflect on how He made sound an accident so that millions can hear the same Quran at once. What does that tell you about His power and His desire to reach every heart? What will you change in your listening habits because of this?

Refutation of an-Nazzam's Theories of Vision
Imam al-Nasafi refutes an-Nazzam's ray and touch theories of vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Nasafi argues that an-Nazzam's theories of vision—the ray as a body and vision by touch—are false.

Core Idea
The ray is an accident, not a body, and touch cannot explain vision.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi directly engages with and refutes two key theories of the Mu'tazili theologian an-Nazzam on how vision works. He first argues that the ray, claimed to be a body connecting eye to object, is actually an accident and thus cannot transfer. Then he argues that if vision were by touch, we would perceive tactile qualities visually. This discussion is important for establishing correct theological and philosophical foundations for sense perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb its structure, then read the English translation to understand the arguments.
Notice the two distinct refutations an-Nazzam's ray theory and his touch theory.
2
Examine the refutation of the ray as a body
Identify the two arguments against the ray: (1) the ray is an accident, so it cannot transfer; (2) if it were a body, instant vision of distant stars would be impossible.
The second argument uses empirical observation of seeing the sky without delay.
3
Examine the refutation of vision by touch
Understand why al-Nasafi argues that if vision were touch, we would perceive tactile qualities (heat, cold, etc.) by sight, which we do not.
He uses the analogy of taste to show that specific sense knowledge remains even when another sense is involved.
4
Consider the final refutation by revelation
Note that al-Nasafi adds that the claim is false by textual evidence (sam‘), showing his method combines reason and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم دعوى النظام اتصال الشعاع وكونه جسما فاسد، لأن الشعاع هو الانجلاء القائم بالبصر، وهو عرض لدخوله تحت حيز الأعراض، والأعراض لا مماسة لها ولا انتقال من محل إلى محل فلا يتصور انتقاله من العين إلى المرئي على أن الشعاع لو كان جسما لكان لا يتصور ما يقول من حيث إن الإنسان يرى السماء وما فيها من الكواكب كلما فتح عينيه من غير تخلل مدة مع بعد ما بينهما، ولا يتصور انتقال جسم في هذه المدة من الأرض إلى السماء مع بعد ما بينهما من المسافة، وكذا لو حصل العلم بالرؤية بطريق المماسة لحصل ما هو المخصوص بالمماسة من العلم بحرارة الممسوس وبرودته ولينه وخشونته ورخاوته وصلابته بمجرد الرؤية، لأن العلم المخصوص بالمماسة لا ينعدم عند وجودها وإن حصل علم آخر وراءه كما في الذوق، فإن العلم المختص بها كذا هذا. ودعواه أن الحواس تدرك بطريق المماسة، دعوى متعرية عن البرهان بل هو باطل، وقد فرغنا الآن عن إبطاله، ثم هو باطل بالسمع.
Then the claim of an-Nazzam about the connection of the ray and that it is a body is false, because the ray is the brightness residing in the eye, and it is an accident because it falls under the category of accidents, and accidents have no touching and no transfer from one place to another; therefore it is inconceivable that it transfers from the eye to the seen object. Moreover, if the ray were a body, it would be inconceivable what he says: that a person sees the sky and what is in it of stars whenever he opens his eyes without any interval despite the distance between them, and it is inconceivable that a body would transfer in that interval from earth to sky with the distance between them. Likewise, if knowledge by vision occurred by way of touching, then that which is specific to touching—knowledge of the heat, cold, softness, roughness, tenderness, and hardness of the touched object—would occur merely by vision, because the knowledge specific to touching is not absent when touching occurs, even if another knowledge is also obtained, as in tasting; for the knowledge specific to it is like this. And his claim that the senses perceive by way of touching is a claim devoid of proof, rather it is false, and we have already finished refuting it. Moreover, it is false by textual evidence.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an-Nazzam's theory of vision. Imam al-Nasafi begins by attacking the claim that vision occurs via a bodily ray that connects the eye to the seen object. He argues that the ray is actually an accident because it is a brightness residing in the eye, and accidents have no touching or transfer between places. Therefore, the ray cannot travel from the eye to the object. He then provides a second argument: if the ray were a body, it would be impossible for a person to see the sky and stars instantly without time delay, given the vast distance. A body cannot travel that fast. Next, he addresses the claim that vision occurs by touching. If that were the case, we would perceive by sight the tactile qualities like heat, cold, etc., which we do not. The knowledge specific to touch does not disappear when touching occurs; rather, it remains alongside other perceptions, as in tasting. Then he dismisses the general claim that senses perceive by touching as baseless and already refuted, and adds that it is also false according to revelation.

الشعاع
الانجلاء
عرض
الأعراض
المماسة
الانتقال
السمع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the ray is a physical body that travels from eye to object.
Correction: The ray is an accident (brightness) residing in the eye; accidents cannot transfer. Moreover, if it were a body, instant vision of distant stars would be impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Nasafi, why can the ray not be a body transferring from eye to object?
A) Because it is an accident and accidents cannot transfer
B) Because the ray is a body that travels instantly
C) Because the eye does not emit anything
D) Because vision is by touch

Key Takeaway
An-Nazzam's theories are logically and theologically untenable; the ray is an accident not a body, and sight does not involve touch.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
An-Nazzam's claim was 'devoid of proof.' In your own life, where might you be holding beliefs about how things work without solid evidence, especially regarding matters of faith? What would it take to subject those beliefs to the same logical scrutiny al-Nasafi applied?

Refutation of an-Nazzam's Claim that Sound is a Body
Refutation of an-Nazzam's body theory of sound.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sound cannot be a body according to kalam, based on the nature of accidents and the phenomenon of multiple simultaneous listeners.

Core Idea
Sound is an accident, not a body, so it cannot transfer.

Imam al-Nasafi here confronts a physical theory that sound is a body moving through the air into the ear. He refutes this by grounding sound in the category of accidents, which by definition cannot transfer. Then he offers a striking thought experiment: a thousand people all hearing the same sound in full — an impossibility for a body. This lesson unpacks his logical critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice the structure: a claim, a refutation based on definition, then a practical argument, then a rhetorical conclusion.
Pay attention to the key term 'الأعراض' (accidents).
2
Identify the three rejected alternatives
The passage considers three ways listeners could hear the sound if it were a body: each hears the whole, each hears a part, or each hears a separate sound. Identify each and note why al-Nasafi rejects it.
These are found in the middle section starting with 'ولا يتصور دخول الجسم...'.
3
Understand the rational intuition argument
Al-Nasafi appeals to 'بديهة العقل' — the rational intuition that each listener knows they hear the full sound. Consider why this is a powerful argument in kalam.
This shows that kalam relies on immediate rational knowledge as a foundation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: إن الصوت جسم ينتقل فيدخل في صماخ السامع باطل، لدخول الصوت تحت حد الأعراض على ما قررنا قبل هذا في أثناء كلامنا، ولا يتصور من الأعراض الانتقال من محل إلى محل ودخولها في محل لأن ذلك من صفات الأجسام. والذي يحقق هذا أن الرجل إذا وجد منه صوت بحضرة ألف نفر اكتشفوه من جوانبه الأربع يسمع كل واحد منهم ذلك الصوت بعينه بكماله، ولا يتصور دخول الجسم في أمكنة كثيرة، ولا يقال: يسمع كل واحد منهم بعضه لأن كل عاقل يعرف ببديهة عقله أنه يسمع كمال صوته ولا يقال: يسمع كل واحد منهم صوتا على حدة لأن كل واحد منهم سمع صوت هذا الرجل ولم يحصل منه إلا صوت واحد. ومن نفسه أنه أراد أن يوهم سمع صوتا سوى الصوت الذي وجد من هذا الرجل لا يقدر ويعرف بنفسه من نفسه الكذب ضرورة الرجوع إلى الحق واتباع أدلته والاقتداء بأهله أولى بالعاقل من ركوب مثل هذه الترهات والوساوس التي لا يخفي فسادها عند التأمل أو إيضاح من تأمل وكشفه عن ذلك على الصبيان والعوام ولكن الله تعالى يكرم بهدايته من يشاء من عباده فضلا منه، ويخذل من يشاء منهم عدلا منه، وهو الغني الحميد يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد لا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ
And his statement that sound is a body that moves and enters the ear of the listener is false, because sound falls under the definition of accidents as we established earlier in our discussion, and it is inconceivable for accidents to transfer from one place to another and to enter a place, because that is a property of bodies. What confirms this is that if a man produces a sound in the presence of a thousand people surrounding him from all sides, each one of them hears that same sound in its entirety. And it is inconceivable for a body to enter multiple places. Nor can it be said that each one hears a part of it, because every rational person knows intuitively that he hears the entirety of the sound. Nor can it be said that each one hears a separate sound, because each one heard the sound of this man, and only one sound came from him. And from himself, if he wanted to pretend to hear a sound other than the sound that came from this man, he would not be able to do so, and he knows from himself the falsehood. Necessity of returning to the truth, following its proofs, and emulating its people is more befitting for the rational person than resorting to such nonsense and whisperings whose corruption is not hidden upon reflection or clarification for the one who reflects and exposes it to children and common people. But Allah Most High honors with His guidance whom He wills of His servants as a favor from Him, and abases whom He wills of them as justice from Him, and He is the Rich, the Praised; He does what He wills and judges what He wills: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned.'
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage refutes an-Nazzam's claim that sound is a body that moves and enters the ear. The author argues that sound is an accident, as defined earlier, and accidents cannot transfer from place to place or enter a place because those are properties of bodies. He then provides a practical proof: if a man makes a sound in front of a thousand people surrounding him, each person hears the same sound in its entirety. It is impossible for a single body to be in many places at once, so sound cannot be a body. Nor is it that each hears a part, because each knows intuitively that he hears the full sound. Nor can each hear a separate sound, because only one sound originated from the man. The author then exhorts the reader to return to truth and follow its proofs, criticizing such futile arguments, and affirms that Allah guides whom He wills, ending with a Quranic verse (21:23) emphasizing His sovereignty.

بديهة العقل
الترهات
الوساوس

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Sound is an accident; accidents cannot transfer; therefore sound is not a body.

Checkpoint

A) Because sound is an accident and cannot transfer
B) Because sound is a body but cannot be in many places
C) Because sound is a spirit
D) Because sound is a quality of the ear

Key Takeaway
Sound is an accident that does not transfer, and the fact that many hear the same sound fully proves it cannot be a body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author says that even children and common people can see the falsehood upon reflection. Where in your own life have you stubbornly held onto an idea despite its clear flaws?
?
'He is not questioned about what He does' – do you truly submit to Allah's decree when your intellect fails to understand His wisdom, or do you secretly demand an explanation before you accept?

The Linguistic Proof Against Identifying Vision with Knowledge
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazilite view and the linguistic proof against it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazilite claim that God's vision is His knowledge is linguistically unsound, using the example of the statement 'I saw it and did not know it.'

Core Idea
Vision and knowledge are distinct; language proves they are not identical.

The Mu'tazilites, including al-Nazzam and al-Ka'bi, argued that God's attribute of vision is actually just His knowledge. In this passage, Nasafi presents a linguistic argument to refute this claim. By testing the everyday statement 'I saw it and did not know it,' he shows that vision and knowledge must be different concepts.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite position
First, read the source passage where Nasafi describes the Mu'tazilite view that vision is a kind of knowledge. Notice how they interpreted God's attribute 'seeing' as merely knowing.
The Mu'tazilites, particularly al-Nazzam and al-Ka'bi, denied that God sees things in a distinct sense.
2
Understand the linguistic test
Nasafi argues that a person can correctly say 'I saw such-and-such and did not know it.' If vision were identical to knowledge, this statement would be contradictory, like saying 'He sat and did not sit.' Recognize why this is a valid test.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why this linguistic fact disproves the Mu'tazilite identification. The ability to affirm vision while denying knowledge shows they are separate meanings.
This proof relies on ordinary language, not technical philosophy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا مسافة بيننا وبينه ولا اتصال شعاع ولا انطباع المرئي في الآلة لتعاليه عن الرؤية بالآلة وهذا ما لا محيص لهم عنه. وتبين بتحقيق رؤية الله تعالى إيانا أن ما وجدوه في الشاهد من أوصاف الوجود لا من أوصاف العلة أو الشرط. جميع وافترقت المعتزلة في الاعتراض على هذا الكلام فأنكر النظام والكعبي من أنه عالم وافقهما أن الله تعالى لا يرى شيئا، وأولوا وصفه تعالى بأنه بصير بالمرئيات وجعلوا الرؤية ضرب علم في الشاهد والغائب جميعا، وإذا كان كذلك كانت رؤيته تعالى إيانا علما منه بنا فلا يشترط هذه الشروط إذ هي من شروط الرؤية دون العلم والرؤية منا وإن كانت علما، ولكن كانت علما مخصوصا حاصلا بهذه الآلة، والعلم بهذه الآلة لا يحصل لنا إلا بهذه الشروط. وهذا فاسد، لأن الرؤية معنى وراء العلم فإن إنسانا لو قال: رأيت كذا ولم أعلم به كان صحيحا، ولو كانت الرؤية هي العلم لصار الرجل نافيا غير ما أثبته وصار مناقضا، كما لو قال: قعد فلان ولم يجلس ولأن محل الرؤية في الشاهد هو العين ومحل العلم هو القلب وهو أمارة التغاير إذ الشيء الواحد لا يحل محلين، وكذا ضد البصر العمى وضد العلم الجهل، وتغاير ضديهما يدل على مغايرتهما. هي طرق معرفة الاتحاد والتعدد، وقد أثبت بكل من ذلك تغايرهما وتعددهما في الشاهد.
There is no distance between us and Him, nor any connection of a ray, nor an impression of the visible object in the organ, because He is exalted above vision by an organ, and this is something they cannot avoid. And it became clear through the verification of God's seeing us that what they found in the witnessed world are attributes of existence, not attributes of cause or condition. All of them—and the Mu'tazilites differed in objecting to this speech—al-Nazzam and al-Ka'bi denied that He is knowing, and both agreed that God does not see anything, and they interpreted His description as 'seeing' as referring to visible things, and they made vision a kind of knowledge in both the witnessed and the unseen. If this is the case, then His seeing us would be His knowledge of us, and these conditions would not be required, for they are conditions of vision, not knowledge; and vision from us, even if it were knowledge, would be a specific knowledge obtained by this organ, and knowledge through this organ is only obtained by us with these conditions. This is corrupt, because vision is a meaning beyond knowledge. If a man said, 'I saw such-and-such and did not know it,' it would be correct. And if vision were knowledge, the man would be negating what he had affirmed and would be contradictory, as if he said, 'So-and-so sat and did not sit.' And because the locus of vision in the witnessed is the eye, and the locus of knowledge is the heart, and this is an indicator of difference, since one thing cannot occupy two loci. Similarly, the opposite of sight is blindness, and the opposite of knowledge is ignorance, and the difference between their opposites indicates their difference. These are ways of knowing union and multiplicity, and by each of them I have established their difference and multiplicity in the witnessed.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that God's vision of things is identical to His knowledge. Nasafi begins by recalling a previous argument: there is no physical distance or medium between God and us, so the Mu'tazilite objection based on bodily vision fails. He then notes that the Mu'tazilites split: al-Nazzam and al-Ka'bi denied that God sees anything at all, while others interpreted God's attribute 'seeing' as merely knowing, making vision a kind of knowledge. Nasafi argues that if vision were identical to knowledge, then the conditions required for physical vision (like distance, a ray, an impression on an organ) would not be relevant, but they are actually conditions of vision, not knowledge. Furthermore, he provides three proofs that vision and knowledge are distinct. (1) Linguistic proof: one can say 'I saw it and did not know it' without contradiction; if they were identical, this statement would be self-contradictory. (2) Locus proof: vision resides in the eye, knowledge in the heart; a single attribute cannot occupy two different loci. (3) Opposite proof: the opposite of vision is blindness, and the opposite of knowledge is ignorance; different opposites indicate different things. Nasafi concludes that vision and knowledge are two distinct entities, as established in the witnessed world, and this refutes the Mu'tazilite identification.

Key Terms
رؤية
علم
بصير
شاهد
غائب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that vision and knowledge are the same because both involve awareness of an object.
Correction: Nasafi shows that language treats them differently: you can see something without knowing it, so they are distinct meanings.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's linguistic argument, why is the Mu'tazilite claim that vision is knowledge false?
A) Because the word 'vision' is never used in Arabic.
B) Because one can correctly say 'I saw it and did not know it.'
C) Because Mu'tazilites rejected all divine attributes.
D) Because knowledge always requires physical conditions.

Key Takeaway
Vision and knowledge are distinct meanings, as shown by the linguistic possibility of affirming one while denying the other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed two things are the same just because they seem related? How does this lesson challenge you to examine your assumptions more critically, especially in matters of faith?
?
When you read verses about God's sight and knowledge, do you conflate them? What would it mean for your understanding of God's attributes if sight and knowledge were identical?
?
The linguistic proof shows that everyday language can reveal profound theological truths. How often do you reflect on the precise meanings of words in your worship and beliefs? Will you commit to being more careful with theological terminology starting today?

Locus and Opposite Proofs for the Distinction of Vision and Knowledge
Nasafi provides locational and oppositional proofs for the distinction of vision and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why vision and knowledge must be distinct based on their different physical loci and opposites.

Core Idea
Different loci and opposites prove vision and knowledge are two different attributes.

After the linguistic argument, Nasafi provides two more proofs that vision and knowledge are distinct. He points out that in the witnessed world, vision resides in the eye while knowledge resides in the heart, and one thing cannot occupy two places. Furthermore, the opposite of vision is blindness, while the opposite of knowledge is ignorance; different opposites indicate different essences.

Guided Path
1
Read the locus argument
Read the part where Nasafi states that the locus of vision is the eye and the locus of knowledge is the heart. Understand why this proves they are different: one attribute cannot be in two different places.
This is an inductive argument from the witnessed world.
2
Read the opposite argument
Then, note that the opposite of sight is blindness, and the opposite of knowledge is ignorance. If vision and knowledge were the same, their opposites would also be the same, but they are not.
3
Synthesize the proofs
Consider how both arguments together strengthen the case that vision and knowledge are two distinct attributes of God, not to be conflated.
Maturidis use such analogical reasoning from the witnessed to the unseen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا مسافة بيننا وبينه ولا اتصال شعاع ولا انطباع المرئي في الآلة لتعاليه عن الرؤية بالآلة وهذا ما لا محيص لهم عنه. وتبين بتحقيق رؤية الله تعالى إيانا أن ما وجدوه في الشاهد من أوصاف الوجود لا من أوصاف العلة أو الشرط. جميع وافترقت المعتزلة في الاعتراض على هذا الكلام فأنكر النظام والكعبي من أنه عالم وافقهما أن الله تعالى لا يرى شيئا، وأولوا وصفه تعالى بأنه بصير بالمرئيات وجعلوا الرؤية ضرب علم في الشاهد والغائب جميعا، وإذا كان كذلك كانت رؤيته تعالى إيانا علما منه بنا فلا يشترط هذه الشروط إذ هي من شروط الرؤية دون العلم والرؤية منا وإن كانت علما، ولكن كانت علما مخصوصا حاصلا بهذه الآلة، والعلم بهذه الآلة لا يحصل لنا إلا بهذه الشروط. وهذا فاسد، لأن الرؤية معنى وراء العلم فإن إنسانا لو قال: رأيت كذا ولم أعلم به كان صحيحا، ولو كانت الرؤية هي العلم لصار الرجل نافيا غير ما أثبته وصار مناقضا، كما لو قال: قعد فلان ولم يجلس ولأن محل الرؤية في الشاهد هو العين ومحل العلم هو القلب وهو أمارة التغاير إذ الشيء الواحد لا يحل محلين، وكذا ضد البصر العمى وضد العلم الجهل، وتغاير ضديهما يدل على مغايرتهما. هي طرق معرفة الاتحاد والتعدد، وقد أثبت بكل من ذلك تغايرهما وتعددهما في الشاهد.
There is no distance between us and Him, nor any connection of a ray, nor an impression of the visible object in the organ, because He is exalted above vision by an organ, and this is something they cannot avoid. And it became clear through the verification of God's seeing us that what they found in the witnessed world are attributes of existence, not attributes of cause or condition. All of them—and the Mu'tazilites differed in objecting to this speech—al-Nazzam and al-Ka'bi denied that He is knowing, and both agreed that God does not see anything, and they interpreted His description as 'seeing' as referring to visible things, and they made vision a kind of knowledge in both the witnessed and the unseen. If this is the case, then His seeing us would be His knowledge of us, and these conditions would not be required, for they are conditions of vision, not knowledge; and vision from us, even if it were knowledge, would be a specific knowledge obtained by this organ, and knowledge through this organ is only obtained by us with these conditions. This is corrupt, because vision is a meaning beyond knowledge. If a man said, 'I saw such-and-such and did not know it,' it would be correct. And if vision were knowledge, the man would be negating what he had affirmed and would be contradictory, as if he said, 'So-and-so sat and did not sit.' And because the locus of vision in the witnessed is the eye, and the locus of knowledge is the heart, and this is an indicator of difference, since one thing cannot occupy two loci. Similarly, the opposite of sight is blindness, and the opposite of knowledge is ignorance, and the difference between their opposites indicates their difference. These are ways of knowing union and multiplicity, and by each of them I have established their difference and multiplicity in the witnessed.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that God's vision of things is identical to His knowledge. Nasafi begins by recalling a previous argument: there is no physical distance or medium between God and us, so the Mu'tazilite objection based on bodily vision fails. He then notes that the Mu'tazilites split: al-Nazzam and al-Ka'bi denied that God sees anything at all, while others interpreted God's attribute 'seeing' as merely knowing, making vision a kind of knowledge. Nasafi argues that if vision were identical to knowledge, then the conditions required for physical vision (like distance, a ray, an impression on an organ) would not be relevant, but they are actually conditions of vision, not knowledge. Furthermore, he provides three proofs that vision and knowledge are distinct. (1) Linguistic proof: one can say 'I saw it and did not know it' without contradiction; if they were identical, this statement would be self-contradictory. (2) Locus proof: vision resides in the eye, knowledge in the heart; a single attribute cannot occupy two different loci. (3) Opposite proof: the opposite of vision is blindness, and the opposite of knowledge is ignorance; different opposites indicate different things. Nasafi concludes that vision and knowledge are two distinct entities, as established in the witnessed world, and this refutes the Mu'tazilite identification.

Key Terms
محل
ضد
عمى
جهل
شاهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because God's attributes are all eternal, distinctions like locus don't apply to Him.
Correction: Nasafi uses the witnessed world as a basis for analogy; if attributes are distinct in creation, they cannot be identical in the Creator without contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what indicates that vision and knowledge are different based on their loci?
A) Both are in the same organ.
B) Vision is in the eye, knowledge in the heart.
C) Neither has a specific locus.
D) Vision can be in the heart.

Key Takeaway
The different loci and opposites of vision and knowledge in the witnessed world confirm that they are two distinct attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though Allah's vision and knowledge are distinct? When you sin in private, do you feel His sight more than His knowledge? Or vice versa? This lesson shows that both are real and distinct—one does not replace the other. How will you cultivate awareness of both?
?
If the opposites of vision and knowledge are blindness and ignorance, then attributing vision and knowledge to Allah means He is free from both. Do you truly exalt Allah above any imperfection? Examine your heart: are there any ways you implicitly limit Allah's perfection by associating Him with qualities of His creation?

Position of the Basran Mu'tazilites on God's Vision
Nasafi introduces the Basran Mu'tazilite position on God's vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Basran Mu'tazilite position that God sees us, but with a distinction from human vision, and how this differs from other Mu'tazilite views.

Core Idea
Basran Mu'tazilites affirm God sees us, but not as we see.

In this passage, Nasafi introduces a key sectarian distinction within Mu'tazilism. While some Mu'tazilites denied that God sees anything, the Basran school conceded that God sees us, but they carefully distinguished His vision from human vision. This distinction is important for preserving divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the concise style and the key terms.
The passage is a fragment, likely the start of a discussion.
2
Identify the key distinction
The Basrans 'differentiate' between God's vision of us and our vision. Consider what this differentiation might entail.
This distinction prevents anthropomorphism.
3
Reflect on the theological context
Contrast this with the position of other Mu'tazilites who deny vision entirely. Why might the Basrans take a middle path?
Think about divine attributes and transcendence.

[God sees us and we do not see Him according to the Basrans]: And the Basrans among them concede that God sees us, but they differentiate between His vision of us

This passage introduces the position of the Basran Mu'tazilites regarding God's vision. Unlike other Mu'tazilites who denied that God sees anything, the Basrans affirm that God sees us. Take five minutes today to silently acknowledge that God is watching — not as a threat, but as a reminder that you are never outside His care.

The Seven Deniers of Prophethood
Lists seven groups that deny the necessity of prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate and understand the arguments of the seven groups that deny the necessity of prophethood according to Imam Nasafi.

Core Idea
Prophethood's opponents can be sorted into seven rational categories.

Imam Nasafi, in his Tabirat al-Adilla, provides a comprehensive classification of those who reject the necessity of prophethood. This enumeration is not mere taxonomy but a tool for understanding the logical structure of the opposition. By examining each group's specific argument, you will see how Islamic theology addresses diverse objections, from metaphysical impossibility to epistemic skepticism.

Guided Path
1
Read the full list
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of all seven groups. Notice the progression from absolute denial to partial acceptance.
The passage is a systematic enumeration.
2
Identify each group's core objection
For each group, note what precisely they deny about prophethood: inherent possibility, necessity of obligation, sufficiency of reason, possibility of miracles, evidential value of miracles, certainty of transmitted reports, or actual occurrence.
3
Compare the differences
Compare how the groups differ in their premises. For example, the first group denies prophethood in itself, while the second permits it but denies obligation.
4
Reflect on purpose
Consider why Imam Nasafi lists these groups. This enumeration helps theologians systematically refute each objection.
The author does not endorse any of these positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويمكن حصر منكري الرسالة في سبع طوائف:
الأولى: أحالها وحكم باستحالتها لذاتها.
الثانية: جوزها ولكن قال : لا تخلو البعثة عن التكليف بأوامر ونواهي والتكليف ممتنع فتنتفى البعثة لانتفاء لازمها.
الثالثة من جوز التكليف وقال : في العقل كفاية في معرفة التكاليف فلا حاجة إلى البعثة بل لا فائدة فيها.
الرابعة : من قال بامتناع المعجزة لأن خرق العادة محال عقلاً ولا تتصور النبوة دونها.
الخامسة من جوز وجود المعجزة لكن منع دلالتها على صدق مدعي النبوة.
السادسة : من سلم دلالتها على صدقه بالنسبة إلى من شاهدها فتفيده العلم بصدقه، ومنع إمكان العلم بها للغائبين عنها فإن العلم بحصول المعجزة لمن غاب عنها إنما يكون بالتواتر وهو لا يفيد العلم أصلا بل الظن، وأنه لا يجدي في المسائل اليقينية.
والطائفة السابعة تعترف بإمكان البعثة وانتفاء الموانع السابقة لكن تمنع وقوع الإرسال.
راجع شرح المواقف للسيد الشريف ج ٣ ص ١٨٣.
It is possible to enumerate the deniers of apostleship in seven groups:
First: Those who deemed it impossible and ruled it impossible in itself.
Second: Those who permitted it but said: the sending cannot be free of obligation with commands and prohibitions, and obligation is impossible, so the sending is negated because its necessary consequence is negated.
Third: Those who permitted obligation and said: reason is sufficient in knowing obligations, so there is no need for sending, rather there is no benefit in it.
Fourth: Those who said that miracle is impossible because breaking custom is impossible rationally, and prophethood cannot be conceived without it.
Fifth: Those who permitted the existence of the miracle but prevented its indication of the truthfulness of the claimant of prophethood.
Sixth: Those who accepted its indication of his truthfulness for those who witnessed it, so it gives them knowledge of his truthfulness, but prevented the possibility of knowing it for those absent from it, because knowledge of the occurrence of a miracle for one absent from it can only be through tawatur (concurrent testimony), which does not give knowledge at all but rather opinion, and that is not useful in certain matters.
And the seventh group acknowledges the possibility of sending and the negation of the previous obstacles but prevents the occurrence of the sending.
Refer to Sharh al-Mawaqif by al-Sayyid al-Sharif, vol. 3, p. 183.
Source pages p. 665

Commentary
This passage is a classification of seven groups that deny the need for prophethood. It lists each group with its specific argument, ranging from deeming prophethood inherently impossible to denying the evidential value of miracles or the occurrence of actual sending. The enumeration is systematic and covers various philosophical and theological objections.

Key Terms

بعثة
تكليف
معجزة
تواتر
ظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Imam Nasafi holds these views himself.
Correction: He is listing objections to be refuted, not stating his own beliefs.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth group, why can't later generations be certain of a miracle?
A) Because miracles are impossible
B) Because concurrent testimony only yields opinion, not certainty
C) Because prophets are untrustworthy
D) Because reason is sufficient

Key Takeaway
The denial of prophethood takes many forms, but each can be systematically addressed through rational and transmitted proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself relying entirely on your own reasoning in a matter of faith, dismissing what Allah has clearly sent through His messengers? What was the result, and how can you commit to submitting to revelation today?
?
When you hear someone say that miracles are impossible because they break natural laws, does that thought ever unsettle you even slightly? How would you answer that doubt with the certainty that comes from this lesson?
?
The seventh group admits that prophethood is possible yet denies it actually happened. Is there any aspect of your faith where you intellectually admit something is possible but fail to fully accept it as real? What step will you take this week to turn that possibility into conviction?

The Khul'aa' Deny Prophethood as Foolishness
Imam Nasafi reports the Khul'aa' argument that prophethood entails safah and bukhl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khul'aa' argument that prophethood entails foolishness and miserliness, and the Islamic response that God's commands are for human benefit.

Core Idea
The Khul'aa' claimed God's commands and prohibitions are pointless—making prophethood foolish.

This passage presents a deviant argument against prophethood from a group called the Khul'aa' (the dissolute). They claim that if prophethood were true, God would be commanding and prohibiting things that do not benefit or harm Him, which they label foolishness and miserliness. The author reports this view and identifies its proponents as those who abandon divine guidance and follow their whims.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the Khul'aa' reason that prophethood entails foolishness (safah) and miserliness (bukhl).
2
Identify the two charges
The argument has two parts: (1) commanding what benefits the commander not is foolish, (2) forbidding what the forbider does not need is miserliness. Locate these in the text.
These are the core of the Khul'aa' case.
3
Understand the implied refutation
Although the passage does not explicitly refute, note that the author describes the group as dissolute and prays for protection from them. This shows the argument is rejected.
The Islamic position is that God's commands benefit humans, not Him.
4
Reflect on the group's traits
Read the description of the Khul'aa'—they cast off obedience and follow whims. The author even warns that some pseudo-Sufis belong to this sect.
This helps recognize deviant claims today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذهبت طائفة إلى أنه لو ثبت لتضمن سفها، إذ (۱) فيه أمر ونهي وتكليف وتحريم وتحليل والله تعالى لا يليق به الأمر والنهي والتحريم، إذ الأمر بما لا نفع في تحصيله للأمر والنهي عما لا ضرر في فعله للناهي سفه، وتحريم ما لا حاجة فيه للمحرم بخل والله تعالى يجل عن السفه والبخل وإلى هذا يذهب طائفة (٢) الناس يسمون الخلعاء الواحد منهم الخليع، وهو الذي خلع عذاره عن ربقة الطاعة وأعرض عما يدعوه (۳) إليه عقله ويزجره عنه وانهمك في شرارته وطغيانه وطاوع هواه ونفسه الأمارة بالسوء في جميع ما يميلان إليه. وعند انكشاف القناع عن مكنون ضمائر كثير من المستتر بالتصوف، وارتفاع الخفاء(4) عن مستور سرائرهم يعلم أنه من هذه الفرقة وهم القائلون بالإباحة طهر الله بلاد الإسلام عنهم وعصم الضعفة من عوام المسلمين عن أنواع مكائدهم وغوائلهم، وصانهم() عن الوقوع في المبثوث من مصائدهم وحبائلهم (٦) .
A group went to the view that if it were established, it would entail foolishness, because it contains command, prohibition, obligation, forbiddance, and permission, and God Almighty is not befitting of command, prohibition, and forbiddance, because commanding what has no benefit in its acquisition for the commander, and prohibiting what has no harm in its doing for the prohibiter, is foolishness, and forbidding what there is no need for in it for the forbidding is miserliness, and God Almighty is exalted above foolishness and miserliness. And this is held by a group of people called the Khul'aa' (dissolute ones), the singular of them is al-khalī' (the dissolute), and he is the one who cast off his rein from the collar of obedience, and turned away from what his intellect calls him to and restrains him from, and immersed himself in his evil and tyranny, and obeyed his whim and his soul that commands evil in all that they incline to. And when the veil is lifted from the hidden consciences of many of those concealing themselves with Sufism, and the concealment is removed from the concealed secrets of their innermost being, it is known that he is from this sect, and they are those who say permissibility (ibāḥa) — may God purify the lands of Islam from them, and protect the weak among the common Muslims from the kinds of their plots and calamities, and preserve them from falling into the widespread of their traps and snares.
Source pages p. 666

Commentary
This passage reports the argument of a group called the Khul'aa' (the dissolute) who claim that if prophethood were established, it would entail foolishness (safah). The author first presents their reasoning: prophethood involves commands, prohibitions, obligations, etc., which are not befitting of God because commanding what benefits the commander not, and prohibiting what harms the prohibiter not, is foolish; similarly, forbidding what the forbider has no need of is miserliness. Since God is above both, prophethood must be rejected. The author then identifies that this view is held by the Khul'aa', describing them as those who cast off restraint and follow their whims. He further notes that many pseudo-Sufis who claim permissibility (ibāḥa) belong to this group, and he prays for God's protection from them.

Key Terms
السفه
البخل
الخلعاء
الخليع
الإباحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's actions must directly benefit or harm Him; otherwise they are pointless.
Correction: God's commands are for the benefit of His creation, not for His own benefit. He is free from need.

Checkpoint
According to the Khul'aa', why is commanding considered foolish?
A) Because it restricts human freedom
B) Because it does not benefit the commander
C) Because it leads to idolatry
D) Because humans cannot understand it

Key Takeaway
The Khul'aa' argued that prophethood entails foolishness and miserliness because God's commands and prohibitions would be purposeless, but this reasoning is false because God's legislation is for human guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Khul'aa' saw God's commands as pointless and burdensome. Is there any command of Allah that you secretly consider pointless or too burdensome? Write down one command you struggle with and commit to obeying it this week, seeking Allah's help.
?
The passage describes the Khul'aa' as those who 'cast off the rein of obedience' and follow their whim. In what subtle ways have you cast off obedience — perhaps by justifying a sin, delaying a duty, or ignoring a prohibition? Repent and resolve to tighten your grip on the rein.
?
The author prays for protection from the plots of the Khul'aa'. Are there any ideas you have absorbed from society or your own nafs that make Allah's commands seem foolish or restrictive? Search your heart and ask Allah to purify it from such thoughts.

The Barahima's Argument Against the Necessity of Prophethood
Imam Nasafi reports the Barahima's proof that reason makes prophethood unnecessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Barahima's reasoning that reason eliminates the need for prophethood, and why they consider sending a messenger to be futile or foolish.

Core Idea
The Barahima argued that if reason already guides us, prophethood is redundant and even foolish.

Imam Nasafi presents the doctrine of the Barahima (Brahmins), a Hindu group who held that human reason is sufficient to know good and evil, and therefore God would not send prophets. This passage outlines their rationalistic challenge to the necessity of prophethood. Understanding their argument is essential for studying Muslim responses in defense of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the formal argumentative style.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage begins with the Barahima's central claim: reason suffices for prophethood. Find how they justify this by saying God placed knowledge of good and evil in reason.
3
Examine the sub-arguments
The passage then gives three additional arguments: 1) Prophethood either agrees or contradicts reason; 2) Sending a messenger who will be rejected is foolish; 3) Preferring some humans without reason is not wisdom. Identify each.
These support the main claim.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this argument would be problematic from an Islamic perspective. Muslims affirm the necessity of prophethood despite reason.
This passage is presented as a view to be refuted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول البراهمة : العقل يغني عن الرسول]: وذهبت طائفة إلى أن الله تعالى على عباده أوامر ونواهي وأفعالهم منقسمة إلى المحاسن والقبائح، والمحاسن مأمور بها والقبائح مزجور عنها. غير أن الله تعالى أودع في عقول البشر العلم بجميع المحاسن وجبلها على الميل إليها، والمعرفة بجميع القبائح وطبعها على النفور عنها، فكانوا مبتلين مكلفين بعقولهم، مأمورين منهيين بها وبالتكليف لهم كفاية، وبالوقوف بعقولهم على جميع ما يحتاجون إليه من المصالح، وقعت لهم الغنية عن الرسالة، فلو أرسل الله إليهم رسولاً وحالتهم هذه، أعني الاستغناء عن الرسل، لفعل ما لا جدوى ولا عاقبة تتعلق به حميده، وما هذا وصفه فهو سفه والله تعالى يجل عن ذلك. وربما يقررون هذا فيقولون بأن الرسالة إما وردت موافقة لما في العقل (۱) ، أو مخالفة له. فإن كانت مخالفة فهي باطلة لأن العقل حجة الله وحججه لا تتناقض. وإن كانت موافقة للعقل فبالعقل عنها غنية فتكون خالية عن الجدوى فيكون عبثًا مع أن إرسال الرسل إلى من يعلم الرسل أنه لا يجيبه إلى ما يدعوه ويقابل رسوله بالتكذيب ويمد يده إليه بالضرب والتعذيب خارج عن الحكمة داخل في حد السفه. ولأنه (۲) لو أرسل لا(۳) فقد فضله على غيره من جنسه، وتفضيل الشيء على ما يجانسه ويساويه في الخلقة ليس بحكمة. وهذه الطائفة هم المعروفون بالبراهمة (٤) وهم قوم ينتسبون إلى الحكمة في الهند ().
The statement of the Brahmins: Reason suffices for prophethood. And a group went to the view that God Almighty has commands and prohibitions for His servants, and their actions are divided into good and evil, and good actions are commanded and evil actions are prohibited. But God Almighty placed in the minds of humans knowledge of all good actions and created them inclined towards them, and knowledge of all evil actions and instilled in them aversion from them. So they are tested and obligated by their minds, commanded and prohibited by them, and by this obligation they have sufficiency, and by their minds grasping all the benefits they need, they become independent of prophethood. So if God sent to them a messenger while they are in this state, meaning independence from messengers, He would do something that has no benefit nor praiseworthy result attached to it, and what is described thus is foolishness, and God Almighty is exalted above that. And perhaps they establish this by saying that prophethood either comes in agreement with what is in the intellect, or in opposition to it. If it is in opposition, then it is false because the intellect is God's proof and His proofs do not contradict. And if it is in agreement with the intellect, then we are independent of it by the intellect, so it becomes devoid of benefit and thus is futile. Moreover, sending messengers to one whom the messenger knows will not respond to what he calls him to and will meet his messenger with denial and extend his hand to strike and torture is outside wisdom and falls within the limit of foolishness. And because if He sent (mark unclear) then He would have preferred him over others of his kind, and preferring a thing over what is similar and equal to it in creation is not wisdom. And this group is known as the Brahmins (Barāhima), and they are a people who trace themselves back to wisdom in India.
Source pages p. 666

Commentary
This passage presents the doctrine of the Barāhima (Brahmins) who argue that reason (al-ʿaql) is sufficient and thus prophethood is unnecessary. The author first states their claim: God has placed in human reason knowledge of all good (maḥāsin) and evil (qabāʾiḥ) and natural inclinations towards good and aversion to evil. Hence humans are obligated solely through reason and have no need for messengers. Sending a messenger would therefore be futile and foolish (safah). Then the author reports their additional arguments: (1) Prophethood either agrees with reason or contradicts it; if it contradicts, it is false (God's proofs do not conflict); if it agrees, reason makes it redundant, so it is futile (ʿabath). (2) Sending a messenger who will be rejected and harmed is unwise. (3) If God sends a messenger, He would be preferring some humans over others without reason, which is not wisdom. The passage ends with identifying these as the Barāhima, a group in India who claim to follow wisdom.

Key Terms
البراهمة
العقل
المحاسن
القبائح
السفه
العبث
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Barahima's argument is an acceptable Islamic view.
Correction: The Barahima are a non-Muslim group from India whose argument against prophethood is presented for refutation by Imam Nasafi.

Checkpoint
What is the central claim of the Barāhima regarding prophethood?
A) Prophethood is possible but unnecessary
B) Reason alone is sufficient and prophethood is therefore superfluous and foolish
C) Prophethood is impossible because God cannot send messengers
D) Prophethood is necessary to confirm rational truths

Key Takeaway
The Barahima argued that reason alone suffices for guidance, rendering prophethood futile, a challenge that Islamic theologians refuted by affirming the necessity of revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your own intellect was sufficient to navigate life's moral challenges, without needing to consult the Quran and Sunnah? What does the Barahima's argument reveal about the danger of such self-reliance?
?
The Barahima said that if prophethood agrees with reason, it is redundant. Do you treat the commands of Allah as optional when they align with your desires, and burdensome when they don't? How would you respond if you were asked to surrender your reasoning to revelation?
?
Consider the Barahima's claim that sending a messenger to those who will reject him is foolish. When you see people rejecting Islam, do you ever question Allah's wisdom in sending prophets? How does this lesson challenge you to trust in Allah's plan even when it seems 'futile' from a human perspective?

Refuting Reason's Self-Sufficiency: The Brahmins' Fallacy
Refutes Brahmins' rationalism via gratitude argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Brahmins' claim that reason alone suffices for moral obligation is invalid in the Maturidi framework, grounded in the inadequacy of reason demonstrated by the gratitude argument.

Core Idea
Reason alone cannot fulfill the infinite demands of gratitude.

The previous lesson established that reason cannot independently determine the proper gratitude owed to Allah, necessitating revelation. Now, Imam al-Nasafi applies that conclusion to refute a specific sect: the Brahmins, who argued that reason is entirely sufficient for moral knowledge and obligation. This passage shows how the gratitude argument directly dismantles their position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Brahmins' claim
Read the passage and identify what the Brahmins are asserting: that reason can know good and evil on its own without revelation, and that intellects are sufficient for taklif.
Their position is a form of rationalism that denies the necessity of prophets for moral guidance.
2
Identify the refutation's basis
Note that the author says 'by this is invalidated'—referring to the previous argument about gratitude. Understand that the refutation relies on establishing reason's limits.
The key is that reason cannot grasp the proper measure of gratitude, which is a moral duty.
3
Connect to the gratitude argument
Recall that the gratitude argument showed reason cannot determine the kind or quantity of gratitude owed to Allah. Hence, revelation is needed. The Brahmins' claim that reason suffices is thus contradicted.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that 'there is no sufficiency at all in that'—reason alone is insufficient. This reinforces the necessity of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا يبطل قول البراهمة القائلين بوقوع الغنية لوقوف العقل على المحاسن والقبائح، وحصول الأمر والنهي بها عن الأوامر الشرعية، وكون العقول كافية للتكليف إذ بينا أن لا كفاية البتة بذلك على ما قررنا من قصور العقول عن الوقوف على ما بينا.
And by this is invalidated the statement of the Brahmins who claim the sufficiency (al-ghunya) due to the intellect's comprehension of good and evil, and the occurrence of command and prohibition by it (the intellect) without need for religious commands (al-awāmir al-sharʿiyya), and that intellects are sufficient for obligation (taklīf), since we have shown that there is no sufficiency at all in that, as we have established from the inadequacy of intellects to comprehend what we have explained.
Source pages p. 684

Commentary
This passage is a concise refutation of the Brahmins' (Barāhima) doctrine that human reason is self-sufficient for moral knowledge and obligation, making revelation unnecessary. The author states that the preceding argument about gratitude decisively disproves their claim. He recaps their position: that reason can independently know good and evil, and thus can generate commands and prohibitions without needing religious laws, and that intellects are sufficient for taklīf (obligation). Then he declares that the previous demonstration (of the inadequacy of reason to determine the proper gratitude, and the need for revealed explanation) shows that there is no sufficiency (lā kifāya) in reason alone. The author thus grounds the necessity of revelation in the inherent limitations of human intellect.

Key Terms
براهمة
غنية
عقل
محاسن وقبائح
أمر ونهي
تكليف
كفاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Brahmins believed that human reason is completely sufficient to know good and evil and to determine moral obligations, making revelation unnecessary.
Correction: The passage refutes this by pointing to the earlier demonstration that reason is inadequate, specifically referring to the inability of reason to determine the proper gratitude owed to Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the key flaw in the Brahmins' claim that reason is sufficient?
A) They deny the existence of God.
B) Reason can only know good but not evil.
C) The previous argument about gratitude demonstrates the need for revelation because reason cannot determine the proper gratitude or its measure.
D) The Brahmins are not monotheists.

Key Takeaway
The Brahmins' claim that reason suffices for moral obligation is refuted by the demonstrated inadequacy of reason to determine the proper gratitude owed to Allah, proving the necessity of revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever relied entirely on your own intellect to decide what is right or wrong, without seeking guidance from revelation? How does this lesson challenge that attitude? What will you do today to actively seek divine guidance in a moral decision you face?
?
Reflect on a blessing for which feel you have not adequately thanked Allah. How does your intellect fall short in recognizing the full extent of gratitude owed? What specific act of gratitude can you perform today that goes beyond your own reasoning?
?
The Brahmins claimed reason suffices, but the lesson shows reason's inadequacy in gratitude. Is there an area of your life where you trust your own reasoning over Allah's commands? What step can you take to surrender that to revelation?

Errors of Pre-Islamic Nations: Indians, Jews, and Christians
Enumeration of errors of three pre-Islamic nations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the errors of pre-Islamic nations—Indians, Jews, and Christians—demonstrate the need for prophetic guidance.

Core Idea
Human reason alone cannot find the truth; prophets are necessary.

Before the advent of Islam, humanity had fallen into deep error. This passage from Imam al-Nasafi describes the misguided beliefs and practices of three major communities: the Indians, the Jews, and the Christians. By seeing their deviations, we understand why Allah sent prophets with clear guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice the three groups mentioned.
The passage is concise—each group is described in a few words.
2
Identify each group's specific error
Find the exact error attributed to the Indians, the Jews (including the 'Ananiyya exception), and the Christians.
Pay attention to the terms: idolatry, anthropomorphism, negation of attributes, tritheism.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: Why does the author list these errors? How does this serve the larger argument of the book?
The author is not merely criticizing; he is showing the need for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجمهور الهند لا يعرفون إلا عبادة الأوثان وإحراق أنفسهم بالنيران. واليهود حرفوا الكلم عن مواضعها ودانوا بالتشبيه المحض إلا العنانية منهم فإنهم يقولون بثبوت الذات، وتعطيل الصفات، وجمعهم تكذيب المسيح عليه السلام. والنصارى متحيرون في دينهم مختلفون في مقالتهم فريق منهم يصف الله تعالى بالصاحبة والولد ، وطائفة منهم يجعلون المسيح (۱) وأمه إلهين من دون الله إلى غير ذلك من المقالات الباطلة والجهالات الفاحشة
The majority of India know nothing but idol worship and burning themselves with fire. The Jews altered words from their places and adhered to pure anthropomorphism, except the 'Ananiyya among them, for they affirm the essence and negate the attributes, and all of them disbelieve in the Messiah, peace be upon him. The Christians are confused in their religion, differing in their opinions: a group among them describe God Almighty as having a companion and a son, and a sect among them make the Messiah and his mother two gods besides God, and other such false statements and foul ignorances.
Source pages p. 745

Commentary
This passage is a description of the state of three major religious communities before the advent of Islam. The author first describes the Indians, who are ignorant of true worship, engaging in idolatry and self-immolation. Then the Jews are described as having altered scripture, falling into extreme anthropomorphism (tashbih) except for the 'Ananiyya sect who affirm God's essence but deny His attributes; all of them reject Jesus. Finally, the Christians are portrayed as divided: some attribute a wife and son to God, others deify Jesus and Mary. The author concludes that these are false statements and foul ignorances, setting up the need for prophetic guidance.

الصاحبة والولد

Misconception: The author is simply insulting other religions.
Correction: The author is describing their errors to demonstrate the need for prophetic guidance.

A) They denied God entirely.
B) They affirmed God's essence but denied attributes.
C) They believed in a human God.
D) They worshipped idols.

Key Takeaway
The errors of pre-Islamic nations highlight humanity's dependence on divine guidance to know the truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the Indians burning themselves for their idols, ask yourself: Are there any beliefs or practices in your life that you cling to even when they harm you, simply because they are familiar? Are you willing to abandon them for the sake of Allah's guidance?
?
The Jews altered God's words. Have you ever found yourself twisting a verse of the Quran to justify your own desires? What would it take for you to submit completely to the text, even when it is hard?
?
The Christians assigned partners to God. Do you ever, even subtly, place something before God in your priorities—like your career, your reputation, or your relationships? How can you realign your heart to give Allah His due alone?

Refuting the Excuse of Warfare for Qur'anic Challenge
Al-Nasafi refutes al-Warraq's claim that wars prevented opponents from challenging the Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi refutes al-Warraq's claim that the polytheists were too occupied with war to respond to the Qur'anic challenge.

Core Idea
The Prophet's thirteen years in Mecca disprove the war excuse.

Al-Warraq, a heretic, argued that the Arabs failed to challenge the Qur'an because they were busy fighting the Prophet. Al-Nasafi counters with a clear historical argument: the Prophet spent thirteen years in Mecca without any warfare, publicly challenging them. This makes the excuse untenable. Let's examine the logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation to get the full argument.
2
Identify the objection
Find al-Warraq's claim in the beginning. Notice how al-Nasafi describes it as ridiculous.
He calls it speech that would amaze people if a madman uttered it.
3
Follow the Meccan phase
The key counterargument: 13 years in Mecca with no war, yet they could not produce a surah.
4
Consider the Medinan phase
After Hijra, only few tribes fought; most Arabs did not, so the excuse still fails.
5
Understand the conclusion
Al-Nasafi calls it manifest impossibility. Only an obstinate opponent would cling to it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض للوراق والرد عليه وما زعم الوراق - بعد انتقاله من مذاهب القدرية إلى مذاهب إخوانهم من الثنوية جريًا منه على قياد ما يفضي إليه -المذهب أن حروبهم معه شغلتهم عن المعارضة كلام لو تفوه به مجنون لتعجب الناس من ذلك، فكيف إذا تكلم به عند المجادلة والمحاجة من يدعي العلم، ويخوض في الكلام، ولكن الغريق يتعلق بكل شيء فنقول له: إنه مكث بمكة ثلاث عشرة سنة يتحداهم بذلك، ويقر عهم آناء الليل والنهار، ويبكتهم في المحافل والمجامع ، وكان انتشر أمره في جميع ديار العرب، وبلغ أقصى نهاية جزيرتها لما كان يعرض نفسه في أيام الموسم على قبائل العرب، ويدعوهم إلى عبادة الله، وينهاهم عما كانوا يدينون به من عبادة الأوثان، ويسفه أحلامهم وأحلام آبائهم الذين كانوا يتفاخرون بمفاخرهم ويتباهون بمناقبهم ومآثرهم، ويتحداهم بالقرآن ويأمرهم بإتيان سورة من مثله، ولم يكن طول تلك المدة بينهم حراب ولا طعان وضراب، فلم لم يعارضوا في تلك المدة وقد تفرغوا له ولم يشغلهم عن ذلك شاغل ولا منعهم عن ذلك مانع ؟! ثم بعدما هاجر إلى المدينة فغزواته معدودة، ومن اشتغل بقتاله من القبائل معروف، وأكثر العرب ما قابلوه بالقتال ولا قاوموه في محال، فما بال أولئك لم يعارضوه في سورة ولم يقابلوه في آيات يسيرة؟!. ثم ما باله لم تشغله تلك الحروب وهو متوحد الذات، وقد شغل جميع العرب مع كثرة ما فيهم من الفصحاء والبلغاء ؟! هذا والله المحال الظاهر الذي لا يتعلق به إلا كل مكابر معاند.
Objection of al-Warraq and the response to it. And what al-Warraq claimed – after his transfer from the doctrines of the Qadariyya to the doctrines of their brethren the Dualists, proceeding according to the lead of what his opinion leads to – that their wars with him occupied them from opposing (the Qur'an) is speech which if a madman uttered it, the people would be amazed at it. How then when one who claims knowledge and engages in discourse (kalam) speaks it in debate and argument? But the drowning man clings to everything. So we say to him: He (the Prophet) stayed in Mecca thirteen years challenging them with that, and reciting to them night and day, and refuting them in assemblies and gatherings. His affair had spread throughout all the lands of the Arabs, and reached the farthest end of its peninsula, as he presented himself in the days of the season to the tribes of the Arabs, calling them to worship God, and forbidding them from what they used to practice of worshipping idols, and belittling their intellects and the intellects of their fathers who used to boast of their glories and take pride in their merits and exploits. And he challenged them with the Qur'an and commanded them to produce a surah like it. And during that entire period there was no warfare, nor stabbing, nor striking between them. So why did they not produce a challenge in that period, when they were free for him, and no preoccupation occupied them from that, nor any preventer prevented them from that?! Then after he migrated to Medina, his military expeditions are counted, and the tribes who engaged in fighting him are known. Most of the Arabs did not meet him with fighting nor resist him in any place. So what is the matter with those people that they did not oppose him in a surah nor confront him with a few verses?! Then what is the matter that those wars did not occupy him while he was unique in person, yet he occupied all the Arabs despite the many eloquent speakers and rhetoricians among them?! This, by God, is the manifest impossibility that only every obstinate opponent clings to.
Source pages p. 750

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection raised by al-Warraq, a heretic who converted from Qadariyya to Dualism. He claimed that the reason the polytheists did not produce a response to the Qur'anic challenge was that they were occupied by the Prophet's military campaigns. The refutation follows a logical argument: First, the Prophet spent thirteen years in Mecca before any warfare occurred. During this period, he publicly challenged them in the season markets, called them to monotheism, ridiculed their idols and ancestors, and demanded they produce a surah like the Qur'an. They had complete leisure and no excuse, yet they failed. Second, after the Hijra, the battles were limited to specific tribes, and most Arabs did not fight at all. So the excuse of war is invalid. The author concludes that such an argument is only clung to by obstinate opponents.

Key Terms
وراق
معارضة
إعجاز
سورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The polytheists could not challenge the Qur'an because they were too busy fighting the Prophet.
Correction: The Prophet spent 13 years in Mecca without war, publicly challenging them. After Hijra, only few tribes fought. The excuse is invalid.

Checkpoint
How many years did the Prophet challenge the Quraysh in Mecca before any warfare?
A) 10 years
B) 13 years
C) 23 years
D) 7 years

Key Takeaway
The excuse of war for failing the Qur'anic challenge is refuted by the historical fact of thirteen peaceful years in Mecca.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have had the Qur'an in your life for years. What surah have you produced? What excuse do you make for not responding to its challenge with your heart and action?
?
If you were among the Quraysh and heard the Prophet's challenge night and day for thirteen years, would you have been too busy with your own 'wars'—your distractions, ambitions, and comforts—to even consider it? What wars are occupying you today?
?
The Prophet was alone yet unoccupied by wars; you are surrounded by the Qur'an yet occupied with everything else. What is the one thing you will change today to begin responding to the Qur'anic challenge?
